<div id="review_2004393008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004393008" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004393008?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004393008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer934878513193356957">If you’re looking for interesting, thought-provoking, hard science fiction, you could certainly do worse than this second novel in the “Uplift Trilogy”. Even though it is the second book in a trilogy, it takes place more than 200 years after the events of book one (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96472.Sundiver__The_Uplift_Saga___1_' title='Sundiver (The Uplift Saga, #1) by David Brin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sundiver</a>) and has no connected story threads or characters so can easily be read without having first read book one. In fact, I recommend doing just that as I believe this novel is a much better introduction to this future universe.<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText934878513193356957" style="display:none">If you’re looking for interesting, thought-provoking, hard science fiction, you could certainly do worse than this second novel in the “Uplift Trilogy”. Even though it is the second book in a trilogy, it takes place more than 200 years after the events of book one (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96472.Sundiver__The_Uplift_Saga___1_" title="Sundiver (The Uplift Saga, #1) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">Sundiver</a>) and has no connected story threads or characters so can easily be read without having first read book one. In fact, I recommend doing just that as I believe this novel is a much better introduction to this future universe.<br /><br />The story takes place on the abandoned ocean world of Kithrup, in the year 2489 AD. The predominantly dolphin-crewed starship <i>Streaker</i> has found sanctuary deep underwater after having found a fleet of abandoned starships in a globular cluster that date back to the time of the fabled “Progenitors”. There is knowledge in this discovery and it turns out that there are races willing to commit murder and even genocide to learn more about the birth of intergalactic civilization. That is a particular problem for the crew of the <i>Streaker</i> because they have been pursued to the planet Kithrup by whole groups of alien starships with dozens of major galactic races now clashing overhead for the right to capture <i>Streaker</i> and her secrets. And just to make things even more interesting, the crew of the <i>Streaker</i> are themselves divided over which course of action to take and, indeed, the planet itself has its own secrets to be dealt with.<br /><br />Try to ignore the fact that this is a novel about “dolphins in space” which, now that I type that, sounds like a silly children’s book title. In the hands of physicist/astrophysicist/futurist David Brin, there is nothing silly about this book. Rather, this is a huge concept novel that serves well to introduce the reader to the concept of “uplift” which is, essentially, the genetic altering of lower species, granting them intelligence, so they can enter Galactic civilization, and achieve star-faring status. Prior to the events of this trilogy, humans have uplifted both dolphins and chimpanzees. It can be a little confusing when reading about dolphins who can speak just as well as humans and I confess to frequently referencing the handy glossary in order to keep straight who’s a human and who’s a dolphin. (There is only one chimp aboard so that one was easy). Brin put a lot of effort into the dolphin society, organization, and language (the dolphins have a haiku-like way of speaking which bridges their primal language of squeaks, clicks and sonar and the human language, "Anglic") and it's extremely convincing.<br /><br />Startide Rising was first published in 1983 and is one of the rare SF novels to 'win the double', securing both the Nebula and Hugo Awards for Best Novel, a feat also achieved by the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234225.Dune__Dune__1_" title="Dune (Dune #1) by Frank Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Dune</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/888628.Neuromancer" title="Neuromancer by William Gibson" rel="nofollow noopener">Neuromancer</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel___1_" title="Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel, #1) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Doomsday Book</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18423.The_Left_Hand_of_Darkness" title="The Left Hand of Darkness by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Left Hand of Darkness</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112537.Rendezvous_with_Rama__Rama___1_" title="Rendezvous with Rama (Rama, #1) by Arthur C. Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">Rendezvous with Rama</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_" title="Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a>. <br /><br />I’ve always wanted to be one of those smart readers who enjoyed hard sci-fi, especially when I was young and tried to compete with my older brother. But usually when I tackled one, I would find my mind wandering off the plot and thinking about other things. It’s not so much that I was bored but I think they tended to be so science-heavy that important story-telling techniques such as relatable characters, intriguing plots, and proper pacing suffered. But I still keep trying once in a while even if I must work up my courage to do so. This novel suffered a little bit of that but my experience this time around was a generally positive one. The ideas were so intriguing, and I really enjoyed the little thought-provoking touches in the story like a dolphin that goes a little off the wire and thinks he is an orca, or the concept of the food chain as a religion. While the novel does feature a lot of science and “future-scientific terms”, in general it was easy enough to follow and the characters were memorable.<br /><br />I do plan to pursue book three, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234489.The_Uplift_War__The_Uplift_Saga___3_" title="The Uplift War (The Uplift Saga, #3) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Uplift War</a> and likely the follow-on trilogy as well.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="934878513193356957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2304615928" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2304615928" />
    <a title="Thom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2945070-thom"><img alt="Thom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422135250p2/2945070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2304615928?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thom" href="/user/show/2945070-thom">Thom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2945070-thom?shelf=fiction-series">fiction-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2304615928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7694352745873461111">In its day, this book won the Nebula, the Locus, and the Hugo awards. It is a sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96472.Sundiver__The_Uplift_Saga___1_' title='Sundiver (The Uplift Saga, #1) by David Brin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sundiver</a>, the second in a trilogy called the Uplift Saga. It was also the sophomore effort by author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14078.David_Brin' title='David Brin' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Brin</a>, and for me, it didn't quite measure up to either the previous book or its own awards.<br/><br/>The universe he created for this series is vast and populated by some really interesting species. This book shows Humankind as the local upstarts, primarily by focusing on one of our client races, the uplifted dolp</span>
  <span id="freeText7694352745873461111" style="display:none">In its day, this book won the Nebula, the Locus, and the Hugo awards. It is a sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96472.Sundiver__The_Uplift_Saga___1_" title="Sundiver (The Uplift Saga, #1) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">Sundiver</a>, the second in a trilogy called the Uplift Saga. It was also the sophomore effort by author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14078.David_Brin" title="David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">David Brin</a>, and for me, it didn't quite measure up to either the previous book or its own awards.<br /><br />The universe he created for this series is vast and populated by some really interesting species. This book shows Humankind as the local upstarts, primarily by focusing on one of our client races, the uplifted dolphins. This story also contains intrigues and politics between the main scientists, at least one of which fits the "mad" description.<br /><br />The story floats through several crewmembers, and while they have their own motivations, they each feel very much the same. Without the vocal stutters, it's hard to tell the 'fins from the humans. This is something many other reviewers have pointed out also.<br /><br />I quite enjoyed the plot - a spaceship forcibly landed on a planet trying to hide from several factions of the various galactic powers, all hunting them for their own reasons of course. How they try to solve this task and what they find on the planet are all a grand story. In fact the whole book fits the genre of "space opera" much more closely than "hard science fiction".<br /><br />The story also stands alone - apparently this trilogy is connected in setting only. A few cameo references are given to the previous novel, and this story takes place quite a bit after.<br /><br />Good plot, flat characters, not as good as the previous effort - this strongly suggests at least some of the awards were more for the author or the first book than this one. I do plan to finish the trilogy as a later book in an "80s challenge" - read one SF book from each year of that decade. But before that I must visit with Vinge, Sagan, Bova, an Bujold. 3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7694352745873461111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_320734332" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/320734332" />
    <a title="Mitchell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/970632-mitchell"><img alt="Mitchell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478717624p2/970632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/320734332?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchell" href="/user/show/970632-mitchell">Mitchell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=author-b">author-b</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=nebula-winner">nebula-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=liked-reviews">liked-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=four-star">four-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=hugo-winner">hugo-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=powellssfgroup">powellssfgroup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970632-mitchell?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320734332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3001934993657558214">Another re-read, this time for powells sf book club. It was especially interesting to re-read this after reading some of my friends negative reviews.<br/><br/>A long time ago I made a list of 10 favorite books of all time in no particular order and this book was on it. It was eventually replaced by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234489.The_Uplift_War__The_Uplift_Saga___3_' title='The Uplift War (The Uplift Saga, #3) by David Brin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Uplift War</a>. I don't recall all the books that were on the list at the time but I know it included <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29946.Illusions_The_Adventures_of_a_Reluctant_Messiah' title='Illusions The Adventures of a Reluctant Messiah by Richard Bach' rel='nofollow noopener'>Illusions: The Adventures of a Reluctant Messiah</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull' title='Jonathan Livingston Seagull by Richard Bach' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2011.The_Dosadi_Experiment__ConSentiency_Universe___2_' title='The Dosadi Experiment (ConSentiency Universe, #2) by Frank Herbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dosadi Experiment</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/776477.Tactics_of_Mistake__Childe_Cycle___4_' title='Tactics of Mistake (Childe Cycle, #4) by Gordon R. Dickson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tactic</a></span>
  <span id="freeText3001934993657558214" style="display:none">Another re-read, this time for powells sf book club. It was especially interesting to re-read this after reading some of my friends negative reviews.<br /><br />A long time ago I made a list of 10 favorite books of all time in no particular order and this book was on it. It was eventually replaced by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234489.The_Uplift_War__The_Uplift_Saga___3_" title="The Uplift War (The Uplift Saga, #3) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Uplift War</a>. I don't recall all the books that were on the list at the time but I know it included <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29946.Illusions_The_Adventures_of_a_Reluctant_Messiah" title="Illusions The Adventures of a Reluctant Messiah by Richard Bach" rel="nofollow noopener">Illusions: The Adventures of a Reluctant Messiah</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Jonathan Livingston Seagull by Richard Bach" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Livingston Seagull</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2011.The_Dosadi_Experiment__ConSentiency_Universe___2_" title="The Dosadi Experiment (ConSentiency Universe, #2) by Frank Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dosadi Experiment</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/776477.Tactics_of_Mistake__Childe_Cycle___4_" title="Tactics of Mistake (Childe Cycle, #4) by Gordon R. Dickson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tactics of Mistake</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/629.Zen_and_the_Art_of_Motorcycle_Maintenance_An_Inquiry_Into_Values" title="Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance An Inquiry Into Values by Robert M. Pirsig" rel="nofollow noopener">Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance: An Inquiry Into Values</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_" title="Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a> - so maybe that says something. And looking at my favorites shelf today I was reminded that it also included <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/353.Time_Enough_for_Love" title="Time Enough for Love by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Time Enough for Love</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28547.Dragonsinger__Harper_Hall___2_" title="Dragonsinger (Harper Hall, #2) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsinger</a>. And maybe <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/667.Anthem" title="Anthem by Ayn Rand" rel="nofollow noopener">Anthem</a>. Or perhaps <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2300.Emergence" title="Emergence by David R. Palmer" rel="nofollow noopener">Emergence</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6421522.Ariel" title="Ariel by Steven R. Boyett" rel="nofollow noopener">Ariel</a>.<br /><br />I've read all of Brin's novels, most of them multiple times, a number of them recently. He doesn't write good endings - he mostly writes non-endings and bad endings. This book has one of his non-endings - or as my dad used to say - is he ever going to get back to the dolphins? This books starts in the middle and ends in the middle.<br /><br />This book starts just after a lot of action which we only get to hear about briefly. Sure it might have made a good book. And yes we do get to watch the crew sitting on the bottom of the ocean doing repairs and slow science for almost the entire book.<br /><br />But we also get to explore language - with Trinary, Anglic and Primary. And the richest set of aliens I've probably seen anywhere. <br /><br />Is this book of product of its time - that is the 80s - specifically the acceptance of workplace harassment? Yes but... So what would have been different if it were written today? There is still workplace romance. There are still crappy coworkers - though mostly this book doesn't support them as doing right. There is some vague homosexuality in a somewhat negative light and limited to the dolphins.<br /><br />In the end this book has a kitchen sink of ideas and ends with a bunch of actual action. For me it holds up to a re-read. And maybe it will be fun to talk about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3001934993657558214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1469303321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469303321" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1433865-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254324661p2/1433865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469303321?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/1433865-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553171709" href="/book/show/1059134.Startide_Rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469303321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5260675476408807042">Initial bad prose and slow pace give way to a serviceable space operatic thriller. There's some irony in humanity being portrayed as having left racism behind when the author only mentions the skin colour of one human character. You guessed it - that person is black. This is subtle, unconscious and no doubt would mortify Brin if ever brought to his attention, but it illustrates that our biases are deep-rooted and often hard to identify in oneself. I say "human character" because there are a majo</span>
  <span id="freeText5260675476408807042" style="display:none">Initial bad prose and slow pace give way to a serviceable space operatic thriller. There's some irony in humanity being portrayed as having left racism behind when the author only mentions the skin colour of one human character. You guessed it - that person is black. This is subtle, unconscious and no doubt would mortify Brin if ever brought to his attention, but it illustrates that our biases are deep-rooted and often hard to identify in oneself. I say "human character" because there are a majority of non-human characters, ranging from genetically enhanced dolphins to numerous aliens. <br /><br />The humans and other Earth-originating species (there's an enhanced chimp as well as all the dolphins) are considered somehow superior to almost all the alien species despite being upstarts, space-faring for mere centuries rather than hundreds of millenia. The main reasons for this are given as being scientists and not relying solely on the technological gifts of our alien neighbours, most of who have stagnated and become wholly reliant on technologies they don't necessarily fully understand, having not developed them but instead taken designs from a ubiquitous Library. I find myself somewhat uncomfortable with this, which is a theme also present in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96472.Sundiver__The_Uplift_Saga___1_" title="Sundiver (The Uplift Saga, #1) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">Sundiver</a> . It smacks of a more subtle version of the vile moral of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/816.Cryptonomicon" title="Cryptonomicon by Neal Stephenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Cryptonomicon</a> i.e. that the USA is superior to everybody else because it expends more time, money, brain power and effort on developing ever-increasingly efficient methods of killing people than others do. The USA has many much more positive things to offer than that. Given the early eighties origin of this book, it could be simply yet another not overly subtle USA vs. the Soviets allegory.<br /><br />Despite all sorts of intrigues, dangers, mysteries (some of which were all too guessable) and adventures, by the end of the book we are not one whit more enlightened about the initiating McGuffin than we were on page one, which is a frustration. This may be an attempt to hook the reader into book three but I still found it frustrating. I was also a bit fed up with all the psychic powers - it's a trope that I am baffled has survived past the psychedelic '60s - it just comes over as silly when there's no attempt to ground it in any type of science.<br /><br />So over-all, it's okay as long as you go along for the roller-coaster ride, which gets to be quite a tense affair, but it doesn't bare much thinking about.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5260675476408807042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mKU4Subg5WAeyG01MB20q0WGeQvw3+GWWx8SzT1M0HLbi+oSPKmI28KFuHJuekyHaHjXTBQ9xNVUMGojvII64Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bBO2TTAWI5+vdmT3xLb4pEhIgQt/jj6h2hAlDt6j4qwvPWQV6l9OJHM7sbCa0QCIZbYvTJtsG+LVP13gX20IPw==')})
  }

When famous adventurer Sir Richard Francis Burton dies, the last thing he expects to do is awaken naked on a foreign planet along the shores of a seemingly endless river. But that\'s where Burton and billions of other humans (plus a few nonhumans) find themselves as the epic Riverworld saga begins. It seems that all of Earthly humanity has been resurrected on the planet, each with an indestructible container that provides three meals a day, cigarettes, alcoholic beverages, a lighter, and the odd tube of lipstick. But why? And by whom? That\'s what Burton and a handful of fellow adventurers are determined to discover as they construct a boat and set out in search of the river\'s source, thought to be millions of miles away. Although there are many hardships during the journey--including an encounter with the infamous Hermann Goring--Burton\'s resolve to complete his quest is strengthened by a visit from the Mysterious Stranger, a being who claims to be a renegade within the very group that created the Riverworld. The stranger tells Burton that he must make it to the river\'s headwaters, along with a dozen others the Stranger has selected, to help stop an evil experiment at the end of which humanity will simply be allowed to die. --Craig E. But who wrote the message and what does it mean? <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2599209964802555595">David Brin is a scientist, speaker, and world-known author. His novels have been New York Times Bestsellers, winning multiple Hugo, Nebula and other awards. At least a dozen have been translated into more than twenty languages.<br/><br/> Existence, his latest novel, offers an unusual scenario for first contact. His ecological thriller, Earth, foreshadowed global warming, cyberwarfare and near-future trends </span>
  <span id="freeText2599209964802555595" style="display:none">David Brin is a scientist, speaker, and world-known author. His novels have been New York Times Bestsellers, winning multiple Hugo, Nebula and other awards. At least a dozen have been translated into more than twenty languages.<br /><br /> Existence, his latest novel, offers an unusual scenario for first contact. His ecological thriller, Earth, foreshadowed global warming, cyberwarfare and near-future trends such as the World Wide Web. A movie, directed by Kevin Costner, was loosely based on his post-apocalyptic novel, The Postman. Startide Rising won the Hugo and Nebula Awards for best novel. The Uplift War also won the Hugo Award.<br /><br /> His non-fiction book -- The Transparent Society: Will Technology Force Us to Choose Between Freedom and Privacy? -- deals with secrecy in the modern world. It won the Freedom of Speech Prize from the American Library Association.<br /><br /> Brin serves on advisory committees dealing with subjects as diverse as national defense and homeland security, astronomy and space exploration, SETI, nanotechnology, and philanthropy.<br /><br /> David appears frequently on TV, including "The Universe" and on the History Channel's "Life After People."<br /><br /> Full and updated at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.davidbrin.com/biography.htm">http://www.davidbrin.com/biography.htm</a></span>

For Streaker carries a cargo of ancient artifacts that may unlock the secret of those who first brought intelligent life to the Galaxies. Many believe a dire prophecy has come to pass: an age of terrifying changes that could end Galactic civilization.\n\nAs dozens of white dwarf stars stand ready to explode, the survival of sentient life in the universe rests on the most improbable dream of all--that age-old antagonists of different races can at last recognize the unity of all consciousness.<\/span>\n  <a
